< text>
The guy who ran the register is pretty rude, doesn't talk much, and will let you wait at the counter for 3-5 minutes. When I'm in a hurry and just want a quick snack and drink that's frustrating. I prefer chevron's because they have friendlier staff and quicker service. This place is run down on the inside and could really use a revamp, not to mention their sketchy gift shop that takes up over half the store. I feel that space could be better ultilized for things that are actually helpful.</text>

When I went to fill my tire the air had leaks in multiple places so I was unable to check the pressure or fill the tire. I told the attendant and he said yeah he knew because everyone told them that it was broken and leaking air. Great, so fix it! California law requires gas stations to provide air and water - it‚Äôs a public safety issue so motorists are not on the roads with flat or low pressure tires!< /Text>

Unfortunately, the shop I had the car towed to after this managed to throw away the old pulley and belt, despite me asking them specifically to save them because of the warranty issue.  G Street Auto said they couldn't do anything about it warranty wise, without seeing the broken components-- which I can understand-- but still, it pretty much sucked for me. <Time>1553017080698< /Time><rating>1<//rating>< Review>
I feel sorry for these folks who appear to have no clue. They seem to be living on the precipice of extinction if my eyes don't deceive me. (Now you are thinking I'm a Silicon Valley entitled brat, and not a senior looking for a good business to support)  I can't imagine how the other reviewers think this place is even "OK". Maybe the loud sports TV is enough?   Rude, and probably stressed, slow service leaves you time to walk down the street to find a rest room, because they claimed to have none!

Possibly good ingredients cooked till dry, and presented with zero panache, but nevertheless strong market pricing .  Dingy, dirty tables, because DIY table prep. alas.  Gas-station style store shelves but without the alluring smell of gasoline, or dazzling illumination to check exactly what's on sale - glad there's nothing unfamiliar.  Pass by and wait less time, in possibly longer lines, down the street.

New enthusiastic management, with customer-oriented eyes to see what I see, could make this the gold mine of Pt Reyes Station.<//Review>

< Review>
I've been coming here for over a year now and always have Max cut my hair. He's a great guy. He remembered my name after the first visit and knows how I want my hair cut without needing any direction.

Every visit, we catch up on the latest sports news, tv shows and movies. It's nice to have someone cut your hair that actually takes the time for small talk. He's always in a good mood. I've been to many places where the stylists act like it's punishment to cut your hair and want to rush through it, often leading to awful haircuts (looking at you Supercuts near AT&T Park).

I live in SF, but make the drive down here for haircuts because of Max and the great prices that are hard to find in the Bay Area ($20 for a men's cut).</Review>

< Review>
I am cancelling my membership with ClubDiscrimination. A few of us parents got together and had one of the members bring a serious matter to the General Manager. The matter being that some members were being permitted to run our children off the courts if they wanted to use the entire court for a pick up game. None of these events were scheduled and my children were their first. The parent, who coaches basketball, whom we had speak to the General Manager, stated that she was only concerned about which set of rules might result in more revenue lost and not at all about making sure that the rules protected all members equally. This General Manager is a serious threat to ClubSport. There is no time that exists to protect my children who are there to train. There is only one rule in place, during all open hours, effecting both courts, to grant all power to members who wish to play pick up. And, there is no rule in place to protect time for the players who pay dues to train there. I pay the same amount of massively high dues that those players play and my kids aren't told to sit at the back of the bus, rather they are told to get off the bus. ClubSport obviously doesn't care at all about our youth sports in Pleasanton. This is truly warped thinking. I plan to take this to their corporate offices, the all forms of media. My kids, are planning to get all their friends together and picket ClubSport at the street entrance. The kids from basketball are angry. It's the basketball courts today and that may not bother you if you don't use them. But, think about the principal. What if tomorrow, you are working out on your favorite cycle, having got to it first. Then a few people walk over & kick you off it, because they claim ClubSport started a new rule that protects groups of 3 & more members training together, to be able to occupy the equipment they want. And so you can be kicked off any equipment any time by equally paying members. Is that really any different? Groups of members may have a good argument why they need to be together and use certain equipment in certain orders. But what makes any members' desires or needs greater than another member's? That's the issue. All equipment, gyms, courts, showers, etc. should be available on a 1st come 1st serve basis. But, ClubSport disagrees with that. They believe that members training for basketball are expendable.<//Review>

< Review>
There isn't any user review about the infant care and I thought my experience can be useful information for others considering the membership.

First off, the nannies don't have a set time of work as in everytime you go in there's a different person taking care of your baby and that could mean longer adjustment time. Most caretakers are young girls which can mean less to zero experience taking care of babies. One time I caught a girl just letting my baby cry out rather than trying to calm him down. And the moment I walked in the front desk employee at club kids and the nanny both had the 'she caught us' expression on their faces.

When you take a tour of the facility they show a tv monitor in the workout floor where you can see how your baby is doing. This monitor is strategically placed far away from the workout area and they have made sure there is only one monitor for the entire facility with really tiny display from each children's area. Meaning they don't want you to keep an eye all the time on what's going on in the baby room.</Review>

This place discriminates against our youth basketball players. You'll be told at sign up that they can play basketball anytime. Yet, they have an old rule that protects the 10-20 older men who want to play a pick-up. The rule states that at ANY time, if 10 players want to have a pick up game, they get to through the other players off the court, who were there first & pay the same money in dues. Furthermore, they can do this on both courts. In short, CS will NOT do anything to protect the rights of their other customers, who might be to small to play with 20-50 year old men, or who might need to just train. They have made a rule to ALWAYS protect the customers who want pick up games & NO rules to protect t the players who want to train. Management has said, "come when pick-up guys aren't here, like at 9:30pm", when most kids are in bed. They refuse to limit that rule to 1 or the 2 courts or limit the amount of time these guys can monopolize it. The GM had a conversation with one of the angry parents, who was told she wouldn't make any changes to the "24-hour ALL encompassing rule" that gives a group of maybe 20 guys, a monopoly & control of the courts, offering NO protection for the other members who pay huge monthly dues. It is an outrage for a GM of a dues based service business, to set up a rule that only protects a small minority and ignores the remaining members. Facilities like this first set rules that protect the interests, access and rights of ALL members. Then if they can implement a rule to help smaller groups, without impacting the access & rights of the client base, then those are looked at. In this case, the absolute reverse was done, except that NO rule was even put in place to protect the client base.. only the small minority group of men who come in every weekday at peak hours, throw everyone off the court & monopolize it for 4 hours. Being made aware of the conversation that took place with the GM, it is clear that the GM felt this was an issue of which way she'll lose more memberships. Bottom line, the rights that were sold to the members are not most important here, not all members are equal and the rules of this place are made to serve the men, with no concern for women and children. Pleasanton is a huge Youth Basketball city... But, this place won't give your kids a place to train. They'll protect the old men playing pick up & tell you to bring your kids when your normally at work or after 9:30pm on a school night. They wouldn't dare tell the old men to come when the courts are empty, during those times....  That would be offensive.... but being offensive to the kids is fine. Unexpected? Yes! Pleasanton is such a kids & family oriented town. Every business caters to families with children. But, while Pleasanton is a kids town, ClubSport isn't. So, just remember that 24 hour fitness is a fraction of the cost of a place that discriminates against our children and where not all members are equal.<//Text>

< text>
Probably the best branch out of all the other ones, now that Clubsport has officially merged with BayClub, Clubsport Pleasanton is spacious, clean, and versatile. It has two large, 25m, multiple-lanes outdoor pools; it operates many indoor tennis courts, along with all the standard equipments that one would expect from a fitness center.

The staff are friendly and courteous, and they even keep your lost items, labbeled and well-kept, for a whole month for the patrons to claim back.

I particularly like the experience of swimming in near freezing temperature in the early morning, and then head straight to the steam room and sauna after a brief shower.

This branch is organized and has everything.</text>

I'm not supporting a place that makes rules to give better access to a few of the guest & not the other guests. That is the definition of discrimination. I read on yelp a letter from CS's manager. He only offered to discuss their programming times. It's clear that he doesn't get how discriminating it is, to make rules that a few people can kick off other people who were there before them, at any time of any day. Yet, the kicked off group, have no time where they can do the same. The rules are 100% set in favor of one group of members. This manger seems to have a conflict of interest somewhere, that someone should expose. He simply side steps the real issues in his reply to a member. But, what is crystal clear, is that he never states that he is sorry for it and will make sure that equal access is guaranteed to both sides. He won't say that, because they maintain that the pick-up members can kick you off at ANY time & off ANY court. He simply asks for a call to try to convince the member that giving access rights to 1 group of members only, is fair & not discriminatory. Also, there are 2 courts. So, the fact that they won't even limit the effect of that rule to 1  court, so that the training members have the other is insane. I have been there so many times to practice my basketball after work. But, I always end up just walking past the courts and on to something else, as the court is being hogged by pick up players. I have also been kicked off the court, along with many other training players, despite having been there 1st, by players getting together a pick up game. I am shocked that such a expensive club would treat its members this way. The norm for clubs is that they refuse to set up rules that will deprive even the very few members of rights, even when it will benefit the vast majority. The understand that NO MEMBER can EVER be DISCRIMINATED against. I suggest they set up a pick-up rule for 1 court & a training rule for the other court.  Sounds fair... right? Not to CS. No, they appear to want 1 sided rules for only select members' use of the gym. As can be seen, they don't really care how many members they offend. I have paid a lot of money to belong to this gym and if I want to train, I have to come during my work hours or when I would normally be going to bed. But the pick-up members have their choice of ANY TIME. So, even if I stated taking off work to come train when no one is there, if suddenly enough guys switched to that time also for a pick-up game, they could again, kick me off the court that I pay to be able to use. I've spoke to members at Club Sport who all also agree that the rule is completely unfair. Especially when those guys hold that court for about 4 hours straight. There must be a reason why certain members get carte blanche at club sport & why the rest of us are told to just be happy with their left overs. No matter what the reason is, this is discrimination! If I had kids trying to train for youth basketball, as other members have complained about, I'd be even that much more angry about it. I invite all who view this to voice your feelings about the overt discrimination going on. Pleasanton is the last city that should ever tolerate this. Well people 24-Hour Fitness is FAR less expensive with NO discrimination. There are also so many other gyms around here. For me, I plan to log complaints with the BBB and others.</Text>

< Review>
My family and I are new members at this facility.  Prior to joining here, I am an active member at 24 Hour Fitness Pleasanton and San Ramon.  Both 24 Hour Fitness facilities offer similar nice amenities most important for me is a lap pool.  It is kept generally clean and the clientele and staff are also generally nice.

With that said, I cannot make a comparison with Club Sport Pleasanton.  Yes, it is a bit pricey, but what CSP offers is beyond gym access.  First of all, if you have kids, then CSP is a better place.  They have activities centered towards children and a pool facility that is kid friendly.   A Family membership provides you a three-hour time for kids to stay at the Kids' area.   There are two separate areas for younger kids and for the bigger kids.

The place is huge but kept very clean!  Even the men's locker room.   The equipment seems to be good and I love the open spaces they have for stretching, etc.  The wall climbing area inside is a cool feature.  The pools, tennis courts, (lots of it), and basketball courts are nice features as well.  Did I mention that the pool is kept at a nice temperature all year round?

On top of the sports equipment, they have bar areas to relax or even do some work.  Yesterday (July 13th) my wife mentioned that while she was there with our kids, she saw a DJ setting up outdoor and she found out that they have dancing later that evening.  So, really, CSP is not just a gym , it is a health and entertainment facility.  It offers a lifestyle not just a place where you go in and out.

I have not been there a lot yet, so I cannot comment about the staff.  So far, I have not experienced any rude ones as some commented here.  All in all, we love this place and will continue to come here.  The price is actually just right for what they offer and for how well they maintain the areas.

Tennis lessons, swimming lessons, and other classes comes with additional fees but really, the price is not much different and perhaps may be better even when you try to sign-up at lessons offered by the Community parks and recreation centers around.

At this point,  I highly recommend to at least give this place a try.  You will not regret it.<//Review>

< review>
Always an easy experience. Always trying to keep the lines down and moving fast. Great selection and helpful staff. It's been my go to grocery store ever since I moved to Napa.

****edited post renovation****
The new renovations completed beginning of 2020 are great. This Lucky now has a self serve salad and hot bar with many options for a quick lunch or dinner. There is seating at the front of the store if you want to eat your food before you leave.Their new frozen entre self serve option seems quite interesting although I have not tried it yet. As always the shelves are neat and faced and full of stock. Lucky prices are higher than other groceries but the shopping experience is above and beyond its competition and, I believe, worth paying a few extra pennies for!</review>
